```text
All four Phase 1 projects are integrated,
all required non-Rive validation is complete,
```

---

# 1. No Clarification Requests

Do not ask the owner:

* how to resolve ordinary merge conflicts;
* whether Harborlight should be included;
* whether migration numbers should be changed;
* whether documentation should be updated;
* whether intended integration files should be committed;
* whether the integration branch should be pushed;
* whether `main` should be fast-forwarded;
* whether the known Rive blocker should stop the merge;
* whether focused tests should be rerun after a repair;
* whether harmless generated files should be removed;
* whether stale integration wording should be corrected.

Those decisions are already authorized by the governing integration prompt.

Use the canonical ownership and conflict-resolution rules in that prompt.

When more than one safe implementation is possible, choose the option that:

1. preserves data;
2. preserves compatibility;
3. maintains one canonical authority;
4. avoids destructive migration;
5. minimizes future technical debt;
6. is easiest to validate;
7. matches existing repository conventions.

Record the decision and continue.

Do not convert ordinary engineering judgment into a human-blocking question.

---

# 2. Continue Through Failures

A failed command is not a stopping point.

When a command fails:

1. capture the exact failure;
2. classify it;
3. identify the root cause;
4. repair the task regression when within scope;
5. run the narrowest focused proof;
6. rerun the failed gate;
7. continue with the remaining operation.

Do not respond with a failure report while the failure is still locally diagnosable and repairable.

Continue through:

* merge conflicts;
* formatting failures;
* lint errors;
* TypeScript errors;
* unit-test failures;
* migration-order failures;
* schema relation failures;
* stale documentation;
* broken imports;
* path-renaming fallout;
* package-script conflicts;
* test-fixture conflicts;
* snapshot mismatches;
* environment-variable schema conflicts;
* build failures caused by integration;
* documentation synchronization failures;
* branch tracking issues;
* non-fast-forward caused by your own local branch state.

Fix them.

Validate the fix.

Continue.

A computer stopping because one comma became emotionally unavailable is not acceptable.

---

# 3. Known Rive Gate Must Not End the Task

The four missing production Rive authoring/export pairs are already known:

```text
invitation seal

```

Their absence remains a truthful Lanternwake release blocker.

It does **not** authorize stopping this four-project mainline integration.

If the repository’s broad validation harness exits early at the Rive asset gate:

1. record the exact known asset failure;
2. do not mark that gate passed;
3. continue by running every remaining non-Rive validation command directly;
4. run the production build directly;
5. run the full unit suite directly;
6. run all four projects’ focused validators directly;
7. run migration rehearsals directly;
8. run repository and build scans directly;
9. run documentation synchronization and validation directly;
10. continue to commit, push, and fast-forward `main` when every non-Rive gate passes.

Do not allow the harness’s early-exit ordering to prevent later independent validation.

The final report must distinguish:

```text
Rive production acceptance: blocked
Four-project Phase 1 mainline integration: completed
```

provided every other required gate passes.

---

# 4. Retry Transient External Failures

For transient failures involving:

* GitHub connectivity;
* DNS;
* package registry access;
* temporary file locks;
* test-server startup;
* occupied validation ports;
* short-lived database locks;
* process shutdown timing;
* remote fetch or push timeouts;

perform bounded retries with diagnosis between attempts.

Use a reasonable progression such as:

```text
attempt 1
diagnose
attempt 2
diagnose and adjust
attempt 3
```

Use another safe port, process, temporary directory, or clean validation worktree where appropriate.

Do not repeatedly issue the identical failing command without learning anything. That is not persistence. That is a shell script reenacting a pigeon flying into a window.

---

---

# 10. Permitted True Stop Conditions

Stop before completion only when continuing would be genuinely unsafe or impossible, such as:

1. `origin/main` contains new work that cannot be reconciled without data loss or incompatible product decisions;
2. required repository credentials or GitHub authorization are unavailable after bounded retry;
3. a required source branch or frozen commit no longer exists remotely;
4. the canonical database cannot be isolated and the next operation would risk production or canonical data;
5. private credentials or real private Chronicle content are discovered in tracked history and continuing would replicate the exposure;
6. migration reconciliation would require destructive loss of unmapped data;
7. a new non-Rive security or privacy regression cannot be safely repaired within the integration scope;
8. GitHub is persistently unavailable and no safe push or mainline update can be performed;
9. repository corruption prevents trustworthy commits.

Before invoking a stop condition:

* exhaust safe local diagnosis;
* attempt bounded recovery;
* preserve all completed work on a local branch;
* push the reviewable branch when remote access permits;
* provide the exact blocking command and evidence;
* explain why no safe autonomous resolution exists.

Ordinary merge conflicts, failed tests, schema mismatches, documentation drift, migration numbering collisions, and known Rive assets are **not** true stop conditions.

---

Do not produce the final response until all of the following are true:

```text
Harborlight is integrated with the existing convergence branch.

The final worktree is clean.
```

The final response must report completed actions, not recommended next actions.

The required final declaration is:

```text
ALL FOUR PHASE 1 PROJECTS INTEGRATED INTO ORIGIN/MAIN
```

Use:

```text

```

only when one of the genuine stop conditions above remains after exhausting every safe autonomous resolution.

Do not begin Phase 2.

Do not wait for the owner to return.

Complete the entire integration and stop only when it is actually done.

const cmd = `@'
import sqlite3
from pathlib import Path
root = Path('prisma/migrations')
db = Path('prisma/phase1-mainline-direct-rehearsal.db')
if db.exists():
    raise SystemExit(f'rehearsal database unexpectedly exists: {db}')
migrations = sorted(root.glob('*/migration.sql'), key=lambda p: p.parent.name)
with sqlite3.connect(db) as connection:
    for path in migrations:
        try:
            connection.executescript(path.read_text(encoding='utf-8'))
        except Exception as error:
            raise SystemExit(f'{path.parent.name}: {error}')
    foreign_keys = connection.execute('pragma foreign_key_check').fetchall()
    tables = {row[0] for row in connection.execute(\"select name from sqlite_master where type='table'\")}
    profile_columns = [row[1] for row in connection.execute('pragma table_info(\"CommunityProfile\")')]
    profile_fks = connection.execute('pragma foreign_key_list(\"CommunityProfile\")').fetchall()
if foreign_keys:
    raise SystemExit(f'foreign key violations: {foreign_keys}')
required = {'CommunityProfile','CommunityListing','CommunityRelease','CommunityAssetReference','CommunityOutboxEvent','UserAccount','Chronicle','PublishedTaleVersion'}
missing = sorted(required - tables)
if missing:
    raise SystemExit(f'missing tables: {missing}')
if profile_columns[:2] != ['id', 'accountId'] or not any(row[2] == 'UserAccount' for row in profile_fks):
    raise SystemExit(f'CommunityProfile canonical relation failed: {profile_columns}, {profile_fks}')
print('ORDERED_MIGRATIONS=' + ','.join(path.parent.name for path in migrations))
print('COMMUNITY_PROFILE_COLUMNS=' + ','.join(profile_columns))
print('COMMUNITY_PROFILE_FK=UserAccount')
print('FOREIGN_KEY_CHECK=PASS')
'@ | C:\\Users\\kgray\\.cache\\codex-runtimes\\codex-primary-runtime\\dependencies\\python\\python.exe -`;
